SUBJECT:
Department of Information Technology – Classification Updates
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve: 1) the new classification of Customer Service Manager; 2) the job specification and salary 
range for the classification of Customer Service Manager; 3) the reclassification of the incumbent in the Technical Support 
Supervisor position to a Customer Service Manager; and 4) the elimination of the Technical Support Supervisor 
classification.
BACKGROUND:
CPS HR Consulting was retained to conduct a classification and compensation study to determine if the incumbent in the 
Technical Support Supervisor position is properly classified. The incumbent in the position is responsible for managing the 
customer service division within the Department of Information Technology, which includes setting organizational 
standards for customer engagement, serving as a communication channel between customers and the Department, and 
ensuring that “first contact” support is provided to customers who need assistance in resolving their technology-related 
problems. The incumbent coordinates and manages citywide information technology (IT) training and communications as 
well as technology-related procurement and vendor contracting, works with the DoIT Director to develop the Department’s 
operational and equipment budgets, tracks and administers approved budgets as assigned, and supervises a team of 
Information Systems Support Technicians who provide direct assistance to customers.
Based on the nature of the work the incumbent performs and the level of the position within the department, CPS HR 
recommends that the City of San Mateo adopt a new classification of Customer Service Manager to appropriately reflect 
the work assigned to the study incumbent. Given the type and level of work the incumbent supervises, CPS HR recommends 
aligning the monthly salary range for Customer Service Manager with that of the GIS Coordinator classification at 
$10,752.04 – $12, 822.11 per month.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The associated salary and benefits for the Customer Service Manager position was included in the 2022-23 budget, so there 
is no budget impact. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
These classification updates are exempt from CEQA review because it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility 
that this activity may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. __ (2023)
CLASSIFICATION UPDATES IN THE DEPARTMENT OF INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY
WHEREAS, pursuant to the San Mateo Municipal Code Section 2.57.030(d), approval of new 
classifications and related job specifications, salary schedules, compensation changes, elimination or 
reinstatement of positions, reallocation of positions, reclassifications, and revisions of job specifications must be 
approved by City Council Resolution; and
WHEREAS, the proposed changes as detailed below are in response to the request from the Department 
of Information Technology to conduct a classification and compensation study of the Technical Support 
Supervisor classification to determine if the incumbent is properly classified and compensated based on the 
level of the position in the department, the nature of the work the incumbent performs, and the type and level 
of the work the incumbent supervises; and
WHEREAS, the proposed job specification for the classification of Customer Service Manager is attached 
hereto as Exhibit A; and the proposed salary range for the classification of Customer Service Manager is 
attached hereto as Exhibit B; and all exhibits are incorporated by reference; and 
WHEREAS, the employee associations representing the impacted classifications have been informed of 
the proposed classification updates and have not brought forth any objections or concerns.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that: 
1.
The classification updates are not subject to California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA Guidelines 
Section 15061(b)(3)) because it can be seen with certainty that they will not cause a physical change 
in the environment; and
2.
The creation of the new classification Customer Service Manager, the job specification and salary 
range for the classification of Customer Service Manager; and
3.
The reclassification of the incumbent in the Technical Support Supervisor position to Customer 
Service Manager, and the elimination of the Technical Support Supervisor classification are 
approved.
68 of 203

--- page 69 ---
Exhibit A
      
CUSTOMER SERVICE MANAGER
DEFINITION
Under administrative direction, plans, organizes, directs, supervises, and controls the operations and 
activities of the Customer Service (Help Desk) division within the Department of Information Technology 
(ITD). An employee in this classification is responsible for overseeing the provision of comprehensive 
end user support, endpoint (e.g., PCs, phones, and mobile) device management, and management of the 
end user training program. This is a managerial classification that describes oversight of professional and 
highly responsive customer service to internal departments and staff following ITD policies and best 
practices.
SUPERVISION RECEIVED AND EXERCISED
Works under the direct supervision of the Director of Information Technology. 
Exercises direct supervision over Customer Service staff.  
EXAMPLES OF ESSENTIAL DUTIES 
Duties may include, but are not limited to, the following:
Plan, organize, direct, and supervise the day-to-day end user support activities of the ITD Customer 
Service division, including the provision of Tier I (initial contact and basic level), Tier II (in-depth level) 
and Tier III (expert level) product and services support; manage the intake and assignment of customer 
support cases, including the administration and maintenance of a customer support case management 
system. 
Plan and participate in the development and implementation of division goals, objectives, policies, and 
priorities; implement City and departmental goals, objectives, policies, and priorities; continually 
collaborate with other IT divisions and City departments to define and direct the best processes and 
practices for delivering quality end user customer support.
Plan and direct the implementation of practices to maximize the efficiency and effectiveness of division 
activities; analyze performance metrics; develop process quality control and improvement processes. 
Serve as a technical consultant to management regarding technical support for computer hardware, 
software, peripherals, and other endpoint devices; perform highly technical work by troubleshooting and 
remediating the most complex end user problems with personal computers, phones, printers, desktop 
69 of 203

--- page 70 ---
software applications, cloud software, and other technology; personally resolve problems and/or 
collaborate with other ITD managers as needed.
Exercise primary responsibility to plan, determine, and manage the appropriate purchasing of computing 
hardware and warranty support in collaboration with other ITD managers and the Director; manage, 
assign, and purchase software subscription licenses for various City software programs; draft 
administrative reports for City Council approval of project selections, including recommendations, 
resolutions, and all supporting documentation.
Manage vendor contracts and agreements related to computing devices, endpoint management services, 
and end user training services; prepare Requests for Proposals or other competitive evaluation processes 
on equipment as required; negotiate contracts for equipment and coordinate the installation of new end 
user-related hardware/software.
Evaluate new computing technologies from various hardware manufacturers to ensure optimal longevity 
for the City; provide endpoint management support for the lifecycle of City computing devices, including 
the management of PC images and provisioning/builds; develop and recommend citywide policies 
addressing acceptable use of City-issued devices, and enforce that usage by ensuring that endpoint 
management tools and agents are installed on all City-owned computing devices.
Administer the budget/purchasing/accounts payable for machinery and equipment, PCs, and maintenance 
of assigned technology systems/products, and participate in annual budget development; engage and 
collaborate with City department managers to forecast the need for computing devices for City staff and 
to develop action plans.
Plan, coordinate, manage, and communicate end user training programs and materials to City staff; select, 
develop, and distribute training materials including all staff email notifications of security concerns, 
training opportunities, and productivity hints/tips; manages contractual relationships with training 
providers. 
Use the customer service case management system to monitor, maintain, measure and report on customer 
service performance; use the case system, surveys, and other tools to produce performance metrics 
including customer satisfaction; ensure all reported customer issues and concerns are addressed in a timely 
manner and work to ensure the end user is satisfied with the outcome.
Supervise, train, develop, and evaluate assigned personnel; schedule, oversee, and assign work activities; 
oversee and manage projects and programs; monitor workflow and productivity; implement employee 
discipline as required; participate in staff selection.
Prepare and present administrative and technical reports and other documents; conduct or review 
feasibility studies; evaluate and provide input to departmental strategic and operational plans.
Schedule and attend meetings and trainings; participate in task forces and committees as assigned.
Perform related duties as assigned.

MINIMUM QUALIFICATIONS
Knowledge of:
Principles, practices, and techniques of business administration, including organizational planning, 
development, budgeting, and quality management.
Desktop computer, virtual and physical server, cloud, and telecommunications technologies, 
including standard local and wide network functions, management information service functions, 
and equipment capabilities.
Fundamentals of information security policies, standards, and practices.
Technology end user support procedures and best practices, including end user case management, 
endpoint provisioning, PC management and maintenance, malware remediation, and maintenance 
of support documentation.
IT vendor management and vendor relations including vendor selection, negotiation, and contract 
management.
Executive/leadership communications, including the drafting of administrative reports.
Principles and practices of employee supervision, including team building, training, personnel 
management, performance evaluation, and employee relations.
Customer service practices, culture, and behaviors.
Techniques and principles of IT project management.
Ability to:
Plan, organize, direct, and supervise the work of technical staff in a manner conducive to high 
performance and personal accountability.
Recommend and implement goals, objectives, and practices for providing effective and efficient 
services.
Review organizational and administrative information, identify problems, make sound policy and 
procedural recommendations, and recommend/implement effective courses of action.
Interpret and apply City and department policies, procedures, and regulations.
Provide advanced computer hardware (PC and laptop) and software support, troubleshooting and 
problem remediation.
Manage projects and meet critical deadlines.
Effectively supervise assigned staff and operations and promote a team environment.
Ensure excellent customer service for all areas of assignment.
71 of 203

--- page 72 ---
Ensure that assigned tasks and projects are completed in a timely manner. 
Communicate clearly and concisely, both orally and in writing.
Maintain effective working relationships with those contacted in the course of work.
Experience and Training
Any combination of experience and training that would provide the required knowledge and abilities is 
qualifying.  A typical way to obtain the required knowledge and abilities would be:
Experience:
Six (6) years of experience providing information technology end user support, including at least 
three (3) year’s comparable to a Senior Information Systems Support Technician in the City of 
San Mateo as well as one (1) year in a lead role that included providing technical and functional 
direction to staff.
Training:
Equivalent to graduation from an accredited four-year college or university with a bachelor’s 
degree in computer science or a related field.
License or Certificate
Possession of, or ability to obtain, a valid California driver’s license.
Microsoft Certified Professional (MCP) desirable.
ADA Special Requirements:
Essential duties require the following physical abilities and work environment:
Ability to work in a standard office environment.

April 17, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Tree Pruning, Maintenance, and Emergency Removal Services Agreement – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the agreement with Peninsula Tree Care, Inc. for tree pruning, maintenance, and emergency 
removal services for an additional $100,000 for a new total agreement amount not to exceed $350,000; and authorize the 
Director of Parks and Recreation to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The Parks and Recreation Department signed an agreement in July 2022 with Peninsula Tree Care, Inc. to provide on-call 
emergency tree maintenance and removal services at a cost of $90 per person hour, up to $95,000. On January 17, 2023, 
City Council approved Amendment No.1 to the agreement, raising the not to exceed amount to $250,000. Due to ongoing 
severe weather (heavy wind and rain), the City needs additional on-call emergency support for tree maintenance and 
removal. Thus, a new not to exceed agreement total of $350,000 is more appropriate based on recent severe storms and 
projected needs.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds in the Tree Division’s operating budget to fund this amendment.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The approval of this amendment is categorically exempt from CEQA because (1) it involves the pruning, maintenance, and
emergency removal of trees for public health and safety purposes, (2) the pruning and maintenance work consists of
minor public alterations in the condition of vegetation which do not involve removal of healthy, mature, scenic trees
except for forestry and agricultural purposes, and (3) the emergency removal of trees is a specific action necessary to
prevent or mitigate an emergency. CEQA Guidelines §15301 (Existing Facilities), Class 1, Subclass (h) (Maintenance of
existing landscaping and native growth); §15304 (Minor Alterations to Land); and §15269 (Emergency Projects).
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
California Board of State and Community Corrections Officer Wellness and Mental Health Program – Grant Appropriation
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to accept and appropriate $75,122.84 received from the California Board of State and Community 
Corrections Officer Wellness and Mental Health Program to the Police Grant Fund Budget for fiscal year 2022-23; and 
authorize the Chief of Police to expend the funds.
BACKGROUND:
The California State Budget Act of 2022 established the Officer Wellness and Mental Health Grant Program, which is 
administered by the Board of State and Community Corrections (BSCC).  The grant program provides $50 million for city 
and county law enforcement agencies for the purpose of improving officer wellness and expanding mental health 
resources.  
The San Mateo Police Department has received an allocation in the amount of $75,122.84.  The funds may be used for a 
variety of purposes related to officer health and wellness.  Upon acceptance and appropriation of funds, staff will solicit 
recommendations from the Police Department Wellness Committee on how these funds should be utilized to best meet 
the needs of officers in our agency, ensuring that any use of funds is consistent with the intended purpose of the grant.
Council approval is requested to appropriate these funds into the Police Grant Fund fiscal year 2022-23 budget.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The BSCC Officer Wellness Grant requires no matching funds and will result in no impact to the General Fund.  Once 
appropriated, $75,122.84 will be added to the Police Grant (Fund 20) budget.  
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
AB 481 Annual Military Equipment Report – Approval  
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve the Annual Military Equipment Report per California Assembly Bill No. 481.
BACKGROUND:
On September 30, 2021, Assembly Bill 481 (AB 481) was codified in Government Code Sections 7070-7075, requiring the 
governing body of law enforcement agencies to adopt a” Military Equipment Use” policy.  The San Mateo Police 
Department presented a policy to the City Council, which was adopted by ordinance on May 2, 2022.
AB 481 also requires law enforcement agencies to prepare an annual report containing information for the preceding 
calendar year.  Staff has prepared a Military Equipment Annual Report (Attachment 1), which summarizes the required 
information including:  a description of the purpose of the equipment and how it was used; any complaints received; the 
results of any internal audits; the cost of the equipment; the quantity possessed; and if the agency intends to acquire 
additional equipment in the next year.  
The San Mateo Police Department does not possess any tactical equipment that it has obtained from the military, nor does 
it possess any equipment that was designed for military use.  The term “military equipment,” as defined in AB 481, 
encompasses many items utilized as component of overall best practices by law enforcement agencies, which are 
employed specifically to reduce risk to community members.  The list includes but is not limited to unmanned aerial or 
ground vehicles, armored vehicles, command and control vehicles, chemical agents, less-lethal shotguns, less-lethal 40mm 
projectile launchers, distraction devices and long-range acoustic devices.  These items provide peace officers the ability to 
safely resolve volatile situations and are vital tools that facilitate compliance with our stringent use of force policy. These 
tools have been tested in the field and are used to enhance citizen and officer safety. 
During the 2022 calendar year, no complaints related to military equipment were received by the Police Department.  
There were no violations of department policy related to the deployment of military equipment by department personnel.  
No new items of military equipment were acquired in the last year; however, the Police Department does intend to 
acquire three (3) additional unmanned aerial system (UAS) devices in the current calendar year, as authorized by the City 
Council on March 20, 2023.  Upon receipt of that equipment, the Military Equipment Use Policy will be updated to reflect 
the addition of those items to the inventory. 
In compliance with AB 481, the Military Equipment Annual Report was published on the Police Department’s website at 
least 30 days prior to this meeting.

SUBJECT:
School Crossing Guards 2023-24 – Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with the San Mateo-Foster City School District for school crossing guards in the amount of $78,000 
and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The annual agreement between the City of San Mateo and the San Mateo-Foster City School District for school crossing 
guards expires on June 30, 2023. The proposed agreement for 2023-24 is included with this report as Attachment 1 and 
continues the City's contribution not to exceed $78,000 towards the cost of crossing guard positions to support the safety 
of San Mateo children.  It is often necessary for the school district to compensate crossing guards for a minimum of 2 or 4 
hours per location in order to attract employees and effectively staff the positions (Exhibit A).  Language has been added 
to the proposed contract to clarify this practice.  Crossing guards are paid $16.75 per hour and will increase per the 
Consumer Price Index (CPI) effective January 1, 2024.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The Police Department has budgeted for this agreement in the proposed 2023-24 budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SCHOOL CROSSING GUARD AGREEMENT 
BETWEEN 
THE CITY OF SAN MATEO 
AND 
THE SAN MATEO-FOSTER CITY SCHOOL DISTRICT 
 
This agreement, made and entered into this day of   
July 1, 2023 
 
           , 
by and between the City of San Mateo, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the 
State of California, hereinafter "City," and the San Mateo-Foster City School District, 
hereinafter "District." 
 
WHEREAS, the City wants to assist the District in providing protection for school 
children who are required to cross heavily traveled streets in the City; and 
 
WHEREAS, some protection can be afforded by placing crossing guards at specific 
locations in the City; and 
 
WHEREAS, the District wishes to cooperate in providing protection for school pupils 
pursuant to Education Code section 45450 et seq., 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, it is agreed as follows: 
 
1. 
The District shall select, hire, and supervise crossing guards as necessary for each 
of the locations shown on Exhibit A to this agreement during the hours that pupils are walking to 
and from nearby schools on school days during the school year.  Salaries and wages shall be at 
rates determined by the District, and may include payment of a two or four hour minimum per 
shift, as shown on Exhibit A, in order to attract employees and effectively staff the positions.  
The crossing guards shall be considered, and shall in fact be, employees of the District for all 
purposes. 
 
2. 
The City agrees to reimburse District for wages and salaries paid by the District to 
the crossing guards for daily administrative costs incurred in providing the crossing guards so 
long as this reimbursement does not exceed that figure agreed to pursuant to paragraph 6 below.  
The reimbursement will include the payment of a two or four hour minimum per shift which will 
be clearly indicated on timecards for such occasions where such payment was necessary to 
effectively staff the position.   
 
3. 
Not later than thirty (30) days after the close of each calendar quarter, the District 
shall bill the City for reimbursement of the costs incurred for work in the previous quarter.  The 
invoice to the City shall be submitted with appropriate supporting documentation such as 
employee time cards and payroll reports to substantiate the amount billed.  Upon review of the 
invoice and supporting documentation, the City shall promptly pay the bill. 
 
4. 
The City and the District shall meet during the month of March of each year 
during the term of this agreement to allocate the City and District portions of the crossing guard 
expense.

At any time during the term of this agreement, the District may request the City to 
delete or add one or more locations from or to the list attached as Exhibit A hereto.  If the City 
determines, pursuant to California Traffic Manual section 10-08.2, that a location either should 
or should not have a crossing guard, the parties may amend this Agreement to add or delete a 
location from Exhibit A.  If a location is added, the District shall promptly provide a crossing 
guard at that location and bill the City appropriately for the location pursuant to this agreement.   
If a location is deleted, the District shall promptly remove the crossing guard and immediately 
cease billing for that location.  During the meeting described in paragraph 4 above, the City and 
the District shall discuss whether any location(s) should be added or deleted.

commensurate with the City’s minimum wage.  On January 1, 2024, the City’s minimum wage 
will increase by CPI and crossing guard wages will be adjusted accordingly.

April 17, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Police Duty Weapon Replacement – Agreements
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing procedure and to approve agreements with LC Action Police 
Supply for $110,092.18 and Stacatto 2011 for $115,201.61 for the procurement of replacement duty weapons for the San 
Mateo Police Department in an amount totaling $225,293.79; and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreements 
in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The San Mateo Police Department provides sworn personnel firearms for duty use. These on-duty service weapons 
generally have a lifespan of 7-10 years as an industry standard.  The duty weapons currently utilized by members of the 
San Mateo Police Department were purchased in 2016.  Last year the handguns were evaluated for serviceability and 
determined to be nearing the end of their useful life and the budgeted replacement has been planned for fiscal year 2023-
24.
Thorough research has been conducted by the San Mateo Police Department’s Firearms Training Unit (FTU), and the Glock 
9mm and Staccato 9mm pistols have been identified as the desired replacement for the current inventory of Glock pistols.  
Instructors from the FTU have fired over 25,000 rounds through several different models of handguns. The new equipment 
was exposed to extreme environmental conditions, tested for compatibility with currently available authorized duty 
holsters, and subjected to a variety of dynamic scenarios.
The proposed new duty weapons include pistol mounted optic technology.  A pistol mounted optic is a device mounted on 
the top of a firearm that emits a red dot only visible to the shooter which allows for pinpoint accuracy and reduces the 
potential of mis-identifying a deadly threat in a critical incident. This technology has become the industry standard due to 
the increase in accuracy and overall safety.
The new and modern equipment will provide law enforcement with several distinct safety advantages benefiting officers 
and the public compared to traditional equipment.  Modernized equipment will allow officers to focus on a threat during a 
stressful situation.  Maximizing accuracy during critical incidents will increase officer safety as well as the safety of our 
community.  
Staff requests approval of the purchase pursuant to SMMC 3.60.070(h)(3), which allows the Council to use any purchasing 
process which is in the best interest of the City.  Pricing for this type of uniform equipment tends to be fairly standardized 
amongst retailers – it is unlikely that putting this purchase out to bid formally would result in significant differences in 
pricing.  LC Action is the only authorized local retailer of the equipment (there are only three authorized retailers in the 
state, with the other two located in Southern California).  Staccato is also the only seller of the Staccato 2011 pistol.  In the 
90 of 203

--- page 91 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
event that items need to be replaced due to a warranty issue or if staff needs to take a piece of equipment in to have it 
repaired or serviced, using a local vendor will allow for this replacement/repair to occur in much more expedient manner.  
Additionally, staff has worked with LC Action and Staccato in the past and has been pleased with their responsiveness and 
customer service.  For these reasons, staff believes it to be in the best interest of the City to proceed with procurement 
from LC Action and Staccato.
BUDGET IMPACT:
Funding for this purchase is available in the Equipment Replacement Fund.  The scheduled year of replacement for duty 
weapons is fiscal year 2023-24; however, due to the lengthy lead-time associated with receiving the items, it is essential 
the order be placed in the current fiscal year to ensure the products are received in time for scheduled Police Department 
training days in September.  The funds will not be spent until the products are received, which will be in fiscal year 2023-
24.  Additionally, the City will receive an estimated $54,000 in revenue upon subsequent sale of the existing duty weapons, 
resulting in a net cost of approximately $171,000.  The new handguns will be placed on a seven (7) year replacement cycle, 
with amortized replacement funds going to the City’s Equipment Replacement Fund.  
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

REPLACEMENT POLICE DUTY WEAPONS AND RELATED EQUIPMENT 
WHEREAS, the duty weapons utilized by the San Mateo Police Department were purchased in 2016 and 
have reached the end of their useful life; and
WHEREAS, thorough research was conducted and the Glock 9mm pistol and the Staccato 9mm pistol 
were identified as the desired replacement handguns; and
WHEREAS, Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3) provides that the City may use any purchasing 
procedures approved by the City Council if the Council makes a finding concurrent with the award that the 
procedures are in the best interest of the City for that particular agreement.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that: 
1.
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity 
that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes to the environment. (CEQA Guidelines 
Section 15378(b)(5).)
2.
Pursuant to Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3), it is found that:
a.
The approval of the agreement to purchase police duty weapons from LC Action is in the 
City’s best interest because LC action is the only authorized local dealer of the equipment, 
thereby allowing for replacement or repairs to be conducted in a more expedient manner, 
because of the general consistency in pricing for these types of goods; and because staff has 
worked with LC action in the past and has been pleased with their responsiveness and 
customer service.
b.
The approval of the agreement to purchase police duty weapons from Staccato 2011 is in 
the City’s best interest because the Staccato pistol has been identified as the desired 
handgun which will best meet the Police Department’s needs and the item is only solid 
directly through the manufacturer. 
3.

Staccato 2011 in the amount of $115,201.61 are approved.

The Chief of Police is authorized to execute the agreements.

within the time specified or to the CITY’s satisfaction the CITY may terminate this Contract or

mediator shall be selected by a "blindfolded" process. 
 
 
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be 
deemed the prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first 
meeting in mediation and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The 
mediation process, once commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement 
is reached by the parties but not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by 
the parties.

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
PURCHASE CONTRACT 
FOR POLICE DUTY WEAPON REPLACEMENT 
FROM STACATTO 2011 
 
 
 
This Purchase Contract (“Contract”), made and entered into this _________day of April 
2023, by and between the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the 
laws of the State of California (“CITY”), and Staccato 2011 LLC, a limited liability company whose 
address is 114 Halmar Cove, Georgetown, TX 78628 (“VENDOR”). 
 
RECITALS: 
 
 
A. 
CITY desires to purchase certain Staccato P DPO pistols and related equipment 
hereinafter described. 
 
 
B. 
CITY desires to engage VENDOR to provide these pistols by reason of its 
qualifications and experience and VENDOR has offered to provide the required goods on the 
terms and in the manner set forth herein. 
 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows: 
 
SECTION 1 - PURCHASE 
 
 
The goods to be purchased from VENDOR under this Contract are described in Exhibit A 
to this Agreement, which is attached and incorporated by reference. 
 
SECTION 2 - PRICE AND TAXES 
 
 
All prices shall be as stated in this Contract and are firm and not subject to escalation.  
This purchase is subject to all California sales tax.  Municipalities are exempt from federal excise 
and transportation taxes.  Prices shall exclude these taxes.   
 
SECTION 3 - PAYMENT 
 
 
Unless otherwise agreed in writing, payment terms shall be net thirty (30) days from 
date of receipt of invoice or acceptance of goods, whichever occurs last.  Invoices must cite the 
purchase order number to prevent delay in payment.  All invoices must be mailed to City of San 
Mateo Police Department, Attn:  Regina Sianez, 200 Franklin Parkway, San Mateo, CA 94403. 
 
100 of 203

--- page 101 ---
SECTION 4 - DELIVERY AND PERFORMANCE 
 
 
Time is of the essence in the performance of this Contract.  If delivery of goods cannot 
be made at the specified time, VENDOR shall promptly notify the CITY of the earliest possible 
date for delivery.  Notwithstanding such notice, if VENDOR for any reason fails to deliver goods 
within the time specified or to the CITY’s satisfaction the CITY may terminate this Contract or 
any part thereof without liability except for goods previously provided and accepted.  The 
CITY’s receipt or acceptance of all or part of a non-conforming delivery shall not constitute a 
waiver of any claim, right or remedy the CITY has under this Contract or applicable law.  
 
SECTION 5 - SHIPMENT AND INSPECTION 
 
 
VENDOR assumes full responsibility for all transportation, transportation scheduling, 
packing, handling, insurance, and other services associated with delivery of all products.  No 
charges for transportation containers, packing, etc., will be allowed the vendor unless so 
specified in this Contract.  All shipments shall be F.O. B. 200 Franklin Parkway, San Mateo, CA 
94403.  Transportation charges shall be shown as a separate item on the invoice. 
 
 
The CITY may revise shipping instructions as to any goods not as yet shipped.  The CITY 
shall have the right to inspect any or all of the goods at VENDOR’s place of business or upon 
receipt by the CITY.  By reason of its failure to inspect the goods, the CITY shall not be deemed 
to have accepted any defective goods or goods which do not conform to the specifications 
provided or to have waived any of the CITY’s rights or remedies arising by virtue of such defects 
or non-conformance.  VENDOR shall be responsible for payment of shipping for the return of 
any defective goods.  Shipping documents and invoices must cite the Purchase Order number. 
 
Pricing must include all charges including handing and delivery.  The handguns should be made 
available for delivery within 60-90 days of receipt of purchase order. 
 
Vendor will provide a master parts list, detailed maintenance, and assembly and disassembly 
manuals.  
 
101 of 203

--- page 102 ---
SECTION 6 - WARRANTIES 
 
 
In addition to any other expressed or implied warranties and unless otherwise agreed in 
writing, VENDOR warrants that all products delivered hereunder will be new, suitable for use as 
described, of the grade and quality specified, free from all defects in design, material and 
workmanship; in conformity with all samples, drawings, descriptions and specifications 
furnished; in compliance with all applicable federal, state and local laws and regulations, and 
free of any liens and encumbrances.  These warranties shall not be deemed to exclude 
VENDOR’s standard warranties or other rights or warranties which the CITY may have or obtain.  
Vendor will provide a twelve (12) month warranty on the handguns, except in the instance of 
abuse. The Vendor agrees he will, at his own expense, provide all labor and parts required to 
remove, repair or replace any defective workmanship and/or materials which becomes or is 
found to be defective during the term of this warranty.  The vendor shall guarantee the 
equipment to be supplied complies with all applicable regulations.  Any weapon returned for 
repair will be given priority and returned to the San Mateo Police Department within ten (10) 
days of receipt. Vendor will supply and guarantee availability of replacement parts at law 
enforcement/dealer pricing.   
 
SECTION 7 - INDEMNITY 
 
 
VENDOR agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense 
arising out of VENDOR’s performance of this Contract, except for those claims arising out of 
CITY’s sole negligence or willful misconduct.  VENDOR agrees to defend CITY, its elected and 
appointed officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. 
 
SECTION 8 - TERMINATION 
 
 
This Contract may be terminated by mutual consent of both parties or by the CITY at its 
discretion.  The CITY may cancel an order for goods at any time with written notice to VENDOR, 
stating the extent and effective date of termination.  Upon receipt of this written notice, 
VENDOR shall stop performance under this Contract as directed by the CITY.  If the Contract is 
terminated, VENDOR shall be paid in accordance with the terms of the Contract for goods 
delivered and accepted.

--- page 103 ---
SECTION 9 - REMEDIES 
 
 
In the event of VENDOR’s breach of this Contract, City may take any or all of the 
following actions, without prejudice to any other rights or remedies available to the City by law:  
(a) require Vendor to repair or replace such goods, and upon VENDOR’s failure or refusal to do 
so, repair or replace the same at VENDOR’s expense; (b) reject any shipment or delivery 
containing defective or nonconforming goods and return for credit or replacement at VENDOR’s 
option, said return to be made at VENDOR’s cost and risk; (c) cancel any outstanding deliveries 
and treat such breach by VENDOR as VENDOR’s repudiation of this contract.  In the event of the 
CITY’s breach hereunder, VENDOR’s exclusive remedy shall be VENDOR’s recovery of the goods 
or the purchase price payable for goods shipped prior to such breach. 
 
SECTION 10 - COMPLIANCE WITH LAW 
 
 
VENDOR warrants that it will comply with all federal, state, and local laws, ordinances, 
rules and regulations applicable to its performance under this Contract.  VENDOR shall obtain 
and maintain throughout the life of the Contract all permits or licenses required in connection 
with the manufacture, sale, and shipment of the products ordered under this Contract.   
 
SECTION 11 - ASSIGNMENT 
 
 
VENDOR shall not delegate or subcontract any duties and services or assign any rights or 
claims under this Contract without the CITY’s prior written consent. 
 
SECTION 12 - ARTWORK, DESIGNS, PATENTS, COPYRIGHTS AND TRADEMARKS 
 
 
VENDOR hereby agrees that the sale, use or incorporation into manufactured products 
of all machines, software, hardware, materials and other devices furnished under this Contract 
are free and clear of infringement of any valid patent, copyright, or trademark.  VENDOR shall 
hold the CITY harmless from any and all costs and expenses, including attorney fees, liability, 
and loss of any kind growing out of claims, suits or actions alleging such infringement, and 
VENDOR agrees to defend such claims, suits or actions. 
 
SECTION 13 - GOVERNING LAW 
 
 
This Purchase Order and the contract between the parties evidenced hereby or attached 
thereto shall be deemed to be made in the State of California and shall in all respects be 
construed and governed by the laws of that state. 
 
SECTION 14 - VENUE 
 
 
In the event of litigation, venue will be in the County of San Mateo.

SECTION 15 - WAIVER 
 
 
The waiver of any term, condition or provision hereof shall not be construed to be a 
waiver of any other such term, condition or provision, nor shall such waiver be deemed a 
waiver of a subsequent breach of the same term, condition or provision. 
 
SECTION 16 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES 
 
 
Attorney fees in an amount not exceeding $85 per hour per attorney, and in total 
amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing of a cost bill) by the 
prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this Contract.  The above 
$5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, appellate court, 
or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It is the 
intent of this provision that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Contract. 
 
SECTION 17 - MEDIATION 
 
 
Should any dispute arise out of this Contract, any party may request that it be submitted 
to mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator 
shall be agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall 
each submit one name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, 
the California State Board of Mediation and Conciliation, or other agreed-upon service.  The 
mediator shall be selected by a "blindfolded" process. 
 
 
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be 
deemed the prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first 
meeting in mediation and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The 
mediation process, once commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement 
is reached by the parties but not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by 
the parties. 
 
SECTION 18 - NOTICES

SUBJECT:
County of San Mateo Human Services Agency – Access and Use Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with the County of San Mateo’s Human Services Agency to allow two licenses to use the Clarity 
Human Services system network, a Homeless Management Information System, by the Police Department’s Homeless 
Outreach Team workers, and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The Police Department maintains a Homeless Outreach Team (HOT), comprised of two civilian employees that conduct 
outreach with the unsheltered population in San Mateo with an end goal of connecting clients with services and long-term 
housing. An integral part of their work consists of coordinating outreach with other local and regional service providers in 
the public and non-profit sectors. Currently, the County of San Mateo Human Services Agency maintains a Homeless 
Management Information System (HMIS) through the Clarity Human Services system network by Bitfocus (referred to 
commonly as “Clarity”). Clarity allows all service providers in the county to communicate and coordinate care for affected 
individuals to achieve optimal outcomes. The County of San Mateo is prepared to grant the HOT two licenses without 
charge to have access to Clarity so they can utilize it when conducting outreach and follow-up care. The access will solely 
be used for homeless outreach services. The terms of the agreement run from April 18th, 2023, through June 30th, 2026. It 
is the City’s policy that City Council approve inter-agency agreements. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no expected budgetary impact from this agreement.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

Clarity Human Services System 
Usage and Data Sharing Agreement Between the County of San Mateo 
Human Services Agency and the San Mateo Police Department
This Usage and Data Sharing Agreement (“Agreement”), entered into this ____ day of April 2023, is between 
the COUNTY OF SAN MATEO HUMAN SERVICES AGENCY (“HSA”) and the SAN MATEO POLICE DEPARTMENT 
(“SMPD”). 
WITNESSETH:
WHEREAS, in 2014, Core Service Agencies and homeless service providers migrated to the secure, private, and 
confidential Clarity Human Services system network by Bitfocus (“Clarity”), a Homeless Management 
Information System (“HMIS”) which allows for data sharing across homeless service providers; and
WHEREAS, the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development’s Homeless Management Information 
Systems (HMIS) Data and Technical Standards Notice, dated July 30, 2004 (“2004 Notice”), seeks to protect 
the confidentiality of personal information while allowing for reasonable, responsible, and limited uses and 
disclosures of data, and the privacy and security standards set forth in the 2004 Notice continue to be 
required in implementing an HMIS; and
WHEREAS, the San Mateo Police Department (“SMPD”) employs two civilian Homeless Outreach Coordinators, 
one full-time and one per diem, to provide homeless outreach services to individuals experiencing 
homelessness in the City of San Mateo; and
WHEREAS, SMPD desires to obtain two Clarity licenses to allow their Homeless Outreach Coordinators to 
enter and access information in Clarity HMIS; and
WHEREAS, the County of San Mateo Human Services Agency (“HSA”) seeks to ensure that any access and use 
of Clarity HMIS is limited to these two SMPD civilian Homeless Outreach Coordinators for the purpose of 
providing homeless outreach services only, and not for any law enforcement, investigation, arrest, 
prosecution, or other penal purpose; 
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS HEREBY AGREED BY THE PARTIES HERETO AS FOLLOWS:
1. Licensing
Only SMPD’s civilian staff who provide safety net or homeless services shall be granted access to Clarity HMIS.  
As of the date of this Agreement, those staff members are identified as follows: 
Victoria Asfour, Homeless Outreach Coordinator (full-time)
David Johnson, Homeless Outreach Coordinator (per diem)
When SMPD requests a Clarity license for a new staff member employed as a 
Homeless Outreach Coordinator, HSA will meet and review with the staff member the 
109 of 203

--- page 110 ---
2
confidentiality and security rules regarding Clarity HMIS.  Any SMPD Homeless Outreach Coordinator granted 
a Clarity license (“SMPD Licensed Staff”) will be required to complete all required Clarity trainings, review and 
accept the Clarity Oath of Confidentiality upon their initial login into Clarity HMIS, and annually thereafter 
while they retain access to the system.  Clarity licenses may not be shared with, used or accessed by anyone 
else, including any other SMPD employees, officers, or command staff who are not SMPD Licensed Staff.  
ACCESS TO CLARITY HMIS AFTER EMPLOYMENT ENDS IS PROHIBITED.  If an SMPD Licensed Staff member 
separates from employment with SMPD, notification must be made as soon as possible to the HSA Service 
Desk ((650) 802-7573, HSAServiceDesk@smcgov.org) in advance of the employee leaving.  The notification 
must provide a license termination date. 
If any license goes unused for more than 90 days, that license may be deactivated.  SMPD Licensed Staff will be 
notified prior to deactivation of the license and shall have 5 business days to respond with a request if the 
license is to be continued.
2. Commitment to Data Entry
SMPD Licensed Staff agree that information they enter into Clarity’s secure system will be timely, accurate, and 
as complete as possible. SMPD Licensed Staff will meet with HSA to establish the plan for what data is entered 
into Clarity for SMPD Licensed Staff.  If SMPD requests that a set of services or programs for SMPD Homeless 
Outreach is created in Clarity, HSA will review and assess the request, and will work with SMPD Licensed Staff 
to determine the most appropriate data structure within Clarity.  SMPD acknowledges that entering data into 
Clarity may impact the County’s federal report submissions, including data quality metrics, and agree that 
SMPD Licensed Staff will follow data entry procedures established by HSA. 
Timely entry of this data is crucial to the community’s ability to match and refer clients to appropriate safety 
net and homeless services provided by other providers; to report accurate performance measures; and to 
capture data on community need.
3. Confidentiality of Client Data
SMPD Licensed Staff will establish appropriate administrative, technical, and physical safeguards to protect the 
confidentiality of client data in Clarity HMIS, and to prevent unauthorized use or access to said data.  
The data in Clarity HMIS shall not be disclosed to anyone or any entity, including but not limited to SMPD 
employees, officers, or command staff who do not possess a Clarity license, or any other law enforcement 
agency, except in connection with the administration of safety net and homeless service programs; as necessary 
to achieve the provision of homeless and safety net services; or for analysis of the data to show performance 
measurements, as permitted by the San Mateo County Clarity HMIS Privacy Policy (“Privacy Policy”).  
Under no circumstances shall the data in Clarity HMIS be used for any law enforcement, investigation, arrest, 
prosecution, or other penal purpose.  A breach of this provision shall result in the immediate termination of 
Clarity licenses granted to SMPD Licensed Staff, and may result in civil damages as well as criminal penalties 
under Federal and State privacy laws.   
110 of 203

--- page 111 ---
3
The data may be reviewed by authorized County personnel to check performance measurements, community 
trends, client services, and for the purpose of monitoring compliance with this Agreement.  Summary results 
(e.g., non-identifying information such as general statistical data, caseload, provider data, funding, and 
expenditure information) is non-confidential and may be shared upon request.  Data that contains identifying 
information will be accessible and shared on a need-to-know basis only, and only to the extent set forth herein 
and as permitted by law.
SMPD and SMPD Licensed Staff acknowledge that this confidential data is proprietary to the County, and 
agree to comply with all applicable State and Federal confidentiality laws and regulations, as well as the 
Privacy Policy.
SMPD Licensed Staff may collect Personally Identifiable Information (“PII”, as defined in federal information 
security and privacy laws as information that can be used on its own or in conjunction with other information 
to identify, contact, or locate a single person, or to identify an individual in context) only when appropriate for 
the purposes for which the information is obtained or when required by law, and not for any law 
enforcement, investigation, arrest, prosecution, or other penal purpose.  SMPD Licensed Staff must collect PII 
by lawful and fair means and, where appropriate, with the knowledge of the individual.  
SMPD Licensed Staff must post the San Mateo County Clarity HMIS Privacy Notice (“Notice”) at each building 
that provides direct services.  If services are being provided in the community or over the phone, SMPD 
Licensed Staff will offer to read the Notice to clients and will also make efforts to provide a written copy of the 
Notice personally, via mail, or other means.  In addition, a copy of the Privacy Policy must be made available to 
clients upon request. Consent of the individual for data collection may be assumed when the Notice is 
properly displayed, read to the client, or a written copy is provided to the client.  Please see the following link 
for a copy of the current Privacy Policy: https://www.smcgov.org/hsa/san-mateo-county-clarity-hmis-privacy-
policy. 
SMPD and SMPD Licensed Staff agree to abide by the Privacy Policy, and agree to further abide by any 
updates to these documents. 
4. Periodic Review
SMPD Licensed Staff shall meet with HSA staff every six months, or more frequently as requested by HSA, to 
discuss the homeless outreach services being provided by SMPD Licensed Staff and interactions with other 
homeless service providers, and to review their use of Clarity HMIS.  These periodic meetings are for the 
purpose of fostering ongoing open communication and partnership between HSA and SMPD Licensed Staff, 
particularly in the event of staffing changes.   
5. Term and Termination
Subject to compliance with all terms and conditions, the term of this Agreement shall be from April 18  ___, 
2023 through June 30, 2026.  This Agreement may only be modified, amended, or extended by written 
agreement of the parties.  This Agreement may be terminated by either party at any time, without a 
requirement of good cause, upon fifteen (15) days’ written notice to the other party.  Should SMPD breach 
any of the terms of this Agreement, the County may terminate the Agreement and SMPD’s access to Clarity 
HMIS immediately. 
111 of 203

--- page 112 ---
4
6. User Support
If SMPD Licensed Staff experience any technical difficulty with Clarity HMIS, they will send a service request to 
the Human Services Agency Business Systems Group at hsa_servicedesk@smcgov.org or (650) 802-7573.
7. SMPD Licensed Staff Responsibilities
SMPD Licensed Staff agree to undergo training and to establish internal processes and procedures to ensure 
that clients’ confidentiality and privacy are safeguarded, and to enter accurate, complete data.  It is 
understood that accessing Clarity HMIS’ secure, private, and confidential system is for the sole purpose of 
serving clients. All SMPD Licensed Staff accessing the Clarity system must have a legitimate business reason 
when searching and accessing information.  All activity in Clarity HMIS is logged, and participating agencies 
understand and agree that this audit trail can be viewed at any time by authorized County personnel.
IN WITNESS OF and in agreement with this Agreement’s terms, the parties, by their duly authorized 
representatives, affix their respective signatures:

SUBJECT:
City of Foster City Usage of Police Firing Range Facilities – Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with the City of Foster City for use of the San Mateo Police Department firing range for an hourly 
rate of $65 with a term through June 30, 2026, and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreement in substantially 
the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
San Mateo is the owner and operator of a firing range located on the police station property at 200 Franklin Parkway. The 
Foster City Police Department desires to use the firing range facilities for the purpose of training and qualifying law 
enforcement personnel in the use of firearms. The term of the proposed agreement is for the period July 1, 2023 through 
June 30, 2026. A fee of $65 per hour will be paid to the City of San Mateo for the use of the range during this period. 
Foster City would remain responsible for providing their own qualified instructor to direct, control, and supervise use of 
the facilities. In addition, any employee using the range will be required to complete and sign a waiver to further release 
the City of San Mateo from any potential liability.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The budget impact for this agreement is minimal, as the revenue generated averages $2,000 per fiscal year.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

AGREEMENT FOR USE OF FIRING RANGE 
 
THIS AGREEMENT is entered into as of   
 
 
 
, by 
and between the CITY OF SAN MATEO ("San Mateo"), a municipal corporation, and 
the CITY OF FOSTER CITY, a municipal corporation ("Contracting Agency"). 
 
RECITALS 
 
WHEREAS, San Mateo owns and operates a firing range; 
 
WHEREAS, Contracting Agency wishes to use the firing range for training, 
competition, and/or other approved purposes; and 
 
WHEREAS, San Mateo desires to allow Contracting Agency to use the firing 
range in accordance with San Mateo's rules and regulations, which are attached as 
Exhibit A and made a part of this Agreement. 
 
AGREEMENT 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration of their mutual covenants, San Mateo and 
Contracting Agency agree as follows: 
 
1. 
San Mateo will allow Contracting Agency to use the firing range for 
training, competition, or other uses authorized by San Mateo. 
2. 
Contracting Agency's use will at all times be under the direction, control, 
and supervision of authorized and qualified Contracting Agency instructors. 
3. 
Use of the firing range is subject to availability in the sole discretion of San 
Mateo. 
4. 
Contracting Agency agrees to pay $65 per hour to San Mateo for the use 
of the range for the effective period of this Agreement.

SUBJECT:
City of San Bruno Usage of Police Firing Range Facilities – Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with the City of San Bruno for use of the San Mateo Police Department firing range for an hourly 
rate of $65 with a term through June 30, 2026, and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreement in substantially 
the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
San Mateo is the owner and operator of a firing range located on the police station property at 200 Franklin Parkway. The 
San Bruno Police Department desires to use the firing range facilities for the purpose of training and qualifying law 
enforcement personnel in the use of firearms. The term of the proposed agreement is for the period July 1, 2023 through 
June 30, 2026. A fee of $65 per hour will be paid to the City of San Mateo for the use of the range during this period. San 
Bruno would remain responsible for providing their own qualified instructor to direct, control, and supervise use of the 
facilities. In addition, any employee using the range will be required to complete and sign a waiver to further release the 
City of San Mateo from any potential liability.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The budget impact for this agreement is minimal, as the revenue generated averages $2,000 per fiscal year.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

SUBJECT:
Kingridge Sewer Line Improvement Mitigation Site Project – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an amendment to the agreement with H.T. Harvey and Associates for environmental engineering services for the 
Kingridge Sanitary Sewer Line Improvement Mitigation Site project at Laurelwood Park in an amount not to exceed 
$24,229, for a total agreement amount of $110,174; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment 
in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
In 2010, Public Works Engineering staff initiated a project to replace the sewer line on Kingridge Drive between 36th and 
42nd Avenue to eliminate sanitary sewer overflows. The project included the replacement of 4,000 feet of pipe, retaining 
walls as slope stabilization measures, and the removal of 17 heritage trees. To conduct the work, regulatory permits were 
obtained from California Department of Fish and Wildlife (CDFW), Regional Water Quality Control Board (RWQCB), and the 
United States Army Corp of Engineers (USACE). As part of the requirements outlined in the environmental permits for the 
sewer improvements, an off-site mitigation area was established at Laurelwood Park to offset the tree removal included in 
the original project, and the Kingridge Sanitary Sewer Mitigation and Monitoring Plan (MMP) was developed. 
H.T. Harvey, an environmental consultant, was hired by Public Works to provide landscaping improvement plans and 
provide six years of long-term maintenance monitoring and habitat development monitoring per the requirements 
outlined in the MMP. The original construction permits needed from the regulatory agencies require a 10-year monitoring 
period. H.T. Harvey recommended that Public Works staff seek an early release from the permit requirements after six 
years of successfully meeting the permit requirements. On behalf of the City, H.T. Harvey requested an early release of 
requirements to CDFW, RWQCB, and USACE after completion of Year 6 but was unsuccessful, resulting in additional 
monitoring through the 10-year term. H.T. Harvey’s original scope of services extend through partial Year 8 but are not 
sufficient to cover work through Year 10. This amendment is to add additional scope and budget to continue monitoring 
services through Year 10 and complete the permit requirements. After successfully completing Year 10, the City will be 
fully released of the permit requirements for the project. 
H.T. Harvey has provided a proposal of $24,229 to provide continued consulting services for the remainder of the 
monitoring and maintenance term for the project. Staff requests approval for Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with 
H.T. Harvey and Associates for environmental engineering services.
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funding for this amendment is available in the Kingridge Sewer (469922) project.

EXHIBIT A2
H.T. HARVEY & ASSOCIATES

Ecological Consultants

PROPOSED SCOPE OF SERVICES
Kingridge Sanitary Sewer Line Project —
Year 8-10 Mitigation Site
Long-Term Monitoring
Proposal # 11173

H. T. Harvey & Associates (H. T. Harvey) is pleased to present this proposal to provide ecological
consulting services to the City of San Mateo’s Department of Public Works for ongoing support for the

Kingridge sanitary sewer riparian mitigation project located in Laurelwood Park, San Mateo, California.

Previous work by H. T. Harvey on this project has been conducted as a sub-consultant to Schaaf & Wheeler as
well as directly contracted to the City of San Mateo Department of Public Works. Our work as a sub-consultant
to Schaaf & Wheeler included nursery coordination and preparation of construction documents. Year 10
long-term monitoring and reporting was previously scoped to H. T. Harvey as a sub-consultant to Schaaf &
Wheeler. However, the Year 10 monitoring and reporting was never billed and the project has since been
closed out. Therefore, we have included Year 10 monitoring and reporting in this proposal. Our more
recent work contracted directly to the City of San Mateo included landscape architecture and ecological
monitoring and reporting services in monitoring Years 1-6. H. T. Harvey used leftover funds from that
contract to continue ecological monitoring in Year 7 and 8 including Year 8 annual vegetation monitoring.
However, these funds will be depleted before Year 8 data analyses and

reporting are completed.

The project's Regional Water Quality Control Board (RWQCB) requires 10 years of long-term
monitoring according to the project’s mitigation and monitoring plan (MMP). Specifically, annual monitoring
and reporting is required in Years 8 and 10. We also believe that a maintenance monitoring event should be
conducted during Year 9 to identify and prompt action to rectify any potential issues that could arise affecting

the site’s ability to meet the final success criteria in Year 10.

Our proposed scope of work includes the following:
e¢ Complete Year 8 long-term data analysis and reporting,
e Year 9 maintenance monitoring and memo preparation,
e Year 10 long-term monitoring and reporting, and

e =Project management.

983 University Avenue, Building D * Los Gatos, CA 95032 © Ph: 408.458.3200

scope of work are as follows.

Task 1. Year 8 Report and Management

H. T. Harvey has conducted Year 8 field monitoring using funding from our previous contract. However,
additional funding is required to finish the data analysis and report writing. H. ‘I’. Harvey will conduct the Year
8 data analysis and reporting of long-term habitat development monitoring per the requirements in the project’s
MMP and RWQCB permit.

Using the data collected and analyzed during the monitoring, described above, H. ‘I. Harvey will generate the
Year 8 annual monitoring report summarizing the project, evaluating the site’s overall performance, and

providing maintenance recommendations.

Maps showing the monitoring site will also be included. Field data sheets will be available for review by the

agencies upon request. The report will be prepared in the following format:

Report Summary

Task 2. Year 9 Maintenance Monitoring and Memo Preparation

In Year 9, Harvey will conduct 1 maintenance monitoring event at the mitigation site in late spring or summer
to assess the condition of the vegetation and to identify issues that could arise affecting the site’s ability to meet
the final success criteria in Year 10, as well as to make any maintenance recommendations. A maintenance
memo will be prepared and submitted to the City including maintenance recommendations to help the project

mect its final success criteria.

e Monthly invoices with billing messages

Task 3. Year 10 Long-Term Monitoring and Reporting

Harvey will conduct Year 10 annual vegetation monitoring per the project’s MMP and the RWQCB permit as

described below:

Plant Survival. Plant survivorship will be determined by counting all of the plants installed. Plant survival will

be tallied by species and for the site as a whole and compared against the final success criterion.

Percent Cover. Percent cover of woody species will be monitored to determine how the site is developing

over time. The percent cover values will be compared to the percent cover final success criterion.

Plant Health and Vigor. The overall health and vigor of plants will be qualitatively monitored by considering
factors such as foliage color, bud development, new growth, herbivory, drought stress, fungal/insect
infestation, and physical damage. The overall health and vigor of all planted woody species will monitored in
Year 10. Plant health and vigor will measured using the numerical and qualitative scale shown in Table 1.
Health and vigor for each woody species will be ascertained by averaging the numerical values for each species.

Plant health and vigor will be assessed for all woody plants installed and compared between years.

H. T. HARVEY & ASSOCIATES

131 of 203


--- page 132 ---
Table 1. Plant Health and Vigor Categories

Qualitative Values Numerical Values Observations

High health and vigor 1-3 67-100% healthy foliage
Medium health and vigor 4-6 34-66% healthy foliage
Low health and vigor 7-9 0-33% healthy foliage

Natural Recruitment. Natural recruitment will be monitored throughout the riparian mitigation site.
Specifically, the number of stems of native and non-native woody plant species observed within a 10-foot band

centered on the percent cover transect were counted and will be reported by species.

Photo Documentation. Photo Documentation of the riparian restoration area will be conducted from a
number of fixed locations. Photographs were also be taken to record any event that may substantially affect
the success of the mitigation, such as flood, fire, or vandalism. These photos will be presented in the Year 10

annual monitoring report.

Other. Significant aspects of site performance and conditions not covered in the formal monitoring plan will
also be monitored. These will include such items as vandalism, irrigation system problems, maintenance

recommendations, and any aspects of the site that may be inhibiting restoration efforts.

Using the data collected and analyzed during the monitoring as described above, H. T. Harvey will generate the
Year 10 annual monitoring report summarizing the project, evaluating the site’s overall performance, and

requesting regulatory agency sign-off. Reporting will mirror that described in Task 1.

By Year 10, it is anticipated that the project will be considered a success by the resource agencies and “signed
off? when the performance criteria are met following the end of the monitoring period. The Year 10 annual

monitoring report will be prepared to establish whether the mitigation site has achieved the success criteria.

A draft report will be submitted to the City by November 15, 2023. After the incorporation of one (1) round
of written comments, the final monitoring report will be prepared. We will submit the final report electronically
as a PDF document to the City. H. T. Harvey will also submit the annual reports to RWQCB. After distribution
of the final report attesting to achievement of the success criteria, H. ‘T. Harvey will coordinate with the
regulatory agencies to confirm completion of the mitigation program. We will then formalize the mitigation

site’s completion in a written letter, and copies will be provided to all participating agencies.

H. 'T. Harvey will maintain communication and coordination with the City throughout the duration of this

project to ensure timely and high quality deliverables.

SUBJECT:
Coyote Point and Poplar Pump Stations Design Services – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 5 to the agreement with Schaaf & Wheeler for additional scope and services for the Coyote 
Point and Poplar Avenue Pump Stations project in an amount not to exceed $89,500 for a total agreement amount of 
$1,407,580; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
Schaaf and Wheeler was hired in August 2014 to provide engineering design services for improvements at the Coyote 
Point Pump Station and Poplar Pump Station (Project). The Project, which included levee improvements, was needed to 
remove North Shoreview and portions of the North Central neighborhoods from the tidal and residual interior Special 
Flood Hazard Areas (SFHA) as shown on the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) Flood Insurance Rate Map. 
The Project is at substantial completion with both pump stations operable and the levee raised to the design elevation. 
Staff is requesting funding for post-construction services for Schaaf and Wheeler to conduct final coordination with FEMA 
on the Letter of Map Revision (LOMR). This process was not originally included in the scope of work and is necessary to 
formally remove the affected homes out of the SFHA for the North Shoreview and portions of the North Central 
neighborhood. Upon approval of the amendment, Schaaf and Wheeler will submit the LOMR to FEMA for review. The 
initial review time is 90 days but may take additional time depending on if revisions are needed. Assuming FEMA 
determines the LOMR complete and accurate, a map revision will be granted.
The additional budget request also includes funding needed for additional inspection work associated with poor soil site 
conditions that were encountered during construction. The unforeseen conditions required a redesign of the foundation 
system and additional time for inspection. 
The amendment increases the agreement by an amount not-to-exceed $89,500 to cover the additional construction work 
and FEMA coordination. Previous amendments are summarized in the table below. 
Original Agreement  
$   546,300
Amendment No. 1-4
$   771,780
Amendment No. 5
$      89,500
Total Agreement
$1,407,580
BUDGET IMPACT:
This amendment will be funded from the North Shoreview Flood Improvements (468202) project.

SUBJECT:
Downtown Parking Equipment Network Hosting and Materials – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 1 for professional services with IPS Group, Inc. to provide parking equipment network hosting 
and materials, increase the agreement amount by $100,000 for a revised agreement total of $400,000, and authorize the 
Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
In June 2021, Council approved an agreement in the amount of $300,000 with IPS Group, Inc. to provide monthly network 
hosting services required by the City’s downtown parking revenue equipment, as well as for providing proprietary parts 
and materials on an as-needed basis to maintain the equipment in good working condition. The funding for the agreement 
also included payment of the credit card transaction fees for each user transaction utilizing credit card payment. 
The agreement estimated the total costs necessary for two (2) years of service. However, additional service and materials 
costs to remove and retrofit pay stations from the downtown area for the pedestrian mall and affordable housing projects 
resulted in higher than anticipated expenses under this agreement. Further, with parking activity increasing to pre-
pandemic levels in the downtown, the cost of the credit card transactions increased beyond what had been included in the 
agreement. This amendment will add an additional $100,000 to provide enough funding for future invoices through the 
original agreement duration (currently expiring in June 2023).  
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding available in the downtown services operations budget for this amendment.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This contract amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that 
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

SUBJECT:
Multihog Compact Multi-Purpose Sweeper – Purchase Contract 
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing procedure; and approve a purchase contract with Municipal 
Maintenance Equipment, Inc. for the purchase of one (1) new Multihog CV 350 Compact Multi-Purpose Sweeper in the 
amount of $173,912.04; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $35,000; and authorize the Public Works 
Director to execute the purchase contract in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The Parks and Recreation Department Parks Division maintains 280,890 square feet of parking lots and pedestrian 
pathways. The proposed purchase of one (1) new Multihog CV 350 Compact Multi-Purpose Sweeper is intended to replace 
an existing 1999 Ford F650 box truck that was used primarily to pull a chipper and haul debris for the Parks Arbor Crew. 
The City no longer employs merit staff to complete tree maintenance and therefore this vehicle does not meet the needs 
of the Department. The proposed sweeper is a more pollution-free and economical solution to the current process.
The Parks Department’s goal is to provide safe and attractive parks while maintaining current levels of debris removal. 
Debris removal is primarily done by gas powered backpack blowers. The proposed multi-purpose sweeper will be used for 
removal of pathway and parking lot debris. The sweeper has certified 4-star containment of pollution, basically eliminating 
the dust levels created by the blowers currently used. Additionally, the proposed sweeper would help create efficiencies in 
staffing, freeing highly-skilled landscape maintenance staff from backpack blower detail. At this time, every park staff 
person has some part of their week dedicated to debris removal. This sweeper will efficiently complete the task of debris 
removal and eliminate more dust than possible with backpack blowers. Staff will continue working on developing the 
infrastructure for electrical leaf blowers. 
As part of the transition to a Green Fleet, staff continually research electrical options during the procurement process and 
aim to replace vehicles with alternative-fueled vehicles when available. The Multihog Multi-Purpose Sweeper is the only 
compact sweeper currently on the market with no electric option available. When an electric version is not available, staff 
evaluates diesel options because the City purchases renewable diesel to replace the use of fossil-based fuel. Renewable 
diesel is made from organic feedstocks and its use reduces carbon emissions. The Multihog Multi-Purpose Sweeper is an 
environmentally-friendly Tier IV diesel engine. Thus, allowing the City to use renewable diesel, which is a non-fossil-based 
option. 
San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3) authorizes the City Council to approve an alternative purchasing 
procedure when it finds doing so is in the best interest of the City. Sourcewell (formerly NJPA) is a government 
organization that solicits, receives, and reviews competitive bids for various specialty equipment, including the Multihog 
CV 350 Compact Multi-Purpose Sweeper. Sourcewell has conducted competitive, public bids to select vendors to achieve 
143 of 203

--- page 144 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
competitive pricing and has selected Multihog as one of their vendors. Municipal Maintenance Equipment, Inc. (MME) is 
the authorized and sole dealership in Northern California for Multihog and will fulfill the purchaser order on behalf of 
Multihog based on the Sourcewell contract.  Therefore, the purchase of one (1) new Mulithog CV 350 Compact Multi-
Purpose Sweeper from MME is in the best interest of the City because the Multi-Purpose Sweeper is the recommended 
replacement for the existing Parks and Recreation truck and the City may rely on bids obtained from Sourcewell because it 
has solicited, received, and reviewed competitive bids for the desired sweeper through its cooperative purchasing 
program. Based on the above, staff recommends the purchase of one (1) new Multihog CV 350 Compact Multi-Purpose 
Sweeper from MME. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Funding for this purchase contract will be funded from the Vehicle and Equipment Replacement Fund. Sufficient funding is 
available.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This purchase is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result 
in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
